SECOND AMENDMENT TO AND RESTATEMENT OF 
JOINT POWERS AGREEMENT ESTABLISHING THE 
PENINSULA TRAFFIC CONGESTION RELIEF ALLIANCE 
 
THIS AGREEMENT by and among the cities and the County of San Mateo who become 
signatories to this agreement (hereinafter referred to as “Party” in the singular and “Parties” 
collectively, as the content requires) is made and entered into as of the _____ day of 
______________, 2021 and in light of the following recitals: 
A. 
The Parties have authority to undertake transportation demand management 
activities in their respective communities and desire to establish and continue the 
Peninsula Traffic Congestion Relief Alliance under which the parties will work 
together essentially to reduce the number of single occupant vehicles traveling on 
streets and highways in San Mateo County. 
B. 
The Parties are authorized to contract with each other for the joint exercise of any 
common power pursuant to Government Code Sections 6500 et seq. 
C. 
The Parties desire to establish and continue the Peninsula Traffic Congestion 
Relief Alliance as a joint powers authority in accordance with the terms and 
conditions outlined in this Agreement and to brand and make this entity known to 
the public as "Commute.org." 
NOW, THEREFORE, the Parties, in consideration of the mutual promises and agreements 
contained herein, agree as follows: 
1. 
Purpose: 
 
 
The Parties enter into this Agreement for the purpose of establishing and 
operating the Peninsula Traffic Congestion Relief Alliance (“Alliance”) to 
reduce traffic congestion and greenhouse gas emissions while enhancing 
the quality of life in San Mateo County by promoting the use of 
sustainable transportation and commute alternatives.  The Parties envision 
a region where all residents and employees have access to equitable, 
sustainable, affordable, and safe transportation options and use them as 
their primary modes when commuting. 
 
2. 
Definitions: 
(a) 
“Employer” shall mean any public or private employer or group 
thereof, including a city or the County, who has a permanent place 
of business in the County of San Mateo.   
114 of 301

--- page 115 ---
768104.4  
2
(b) 
“Party” or “Parties” shall mean a member of the Peninsula Traffic 
Congestion Relief Alliance and a party signator to this Agreement 
establishing the Alliance. 
(c) 
“TDM or Transportation Demand Management” shall mean a 
program or activity to improve the efficiency of the existing 
transportation system by increasing the use of alternative modes of 
transportation such as carpools, vanpools, public transit, bicycles, 
walking and telecommuting.   
3. 
Establishment of Alliance:  The Parties hereby create an entity originally 
called the Peninsula Traffic Congestion Relief Alliance to exercise in the 
manner set forth in this Agreement the specified powers common to each 
of the Parties.  For purposes of name identification and branding, the 
Alliance shall be known to the public as "Commute.org."  The Alliance 
shall be a public entity that is separate from the Parties and shall be 
responsible for the administration of this Agreement.  Except as provided 
herein, the debts, liabilities, and/or obligations of the Alliance shall be the 
debts, liabilities, and/or obligations solely of the Alliance and shall not be 
the debts, liabilities, and/or obligations of any Party to this Agreement. 
4. 
Term:  This Agreement shall be effective on the date by which any nine 
Parties have executed it and shall continue in effect until terminated as 
provided herein. 
5. 
Powers of the Alliance:  The Alliance shall have the powers and duties: 
(a) 
To make and enter into contracts;  
(b) 
To incur debts, liabilities or obligations; 
(c) 
To solicit, receive, and use grants, advances and contributions from 
all available sources, public or private, including federal, state and 
local subventions;  
(d) 
To adopt bylaws;  
(e) 
To employ employees or agents or contract for the services of 
agents, employees, consultants and such other persons or firms as 
it deems necessary;  
(f) 
To sue and be sued in its own name; 
(g) 
To invest any surplus funds not required for the immediate 
necessities of the Alliance as the Governing Board determines is 
advisable, in the same manner and upon the same conditions as 
local agencies pursuant to Government Code Section 53601;

--- page 116 ---
768104.4  
3
(h) 
To enforce all provisions of this Agreement; 
(i) 
To negotiate for, acquire, hold, manage, maintain, control or 
dispose of real and personal property;  
(j) 
To levy and collect fees and charges, including administrative and 
operating costs, to third parties who receive the benefit of services 
from the Alliance; and 
(k) 
To do all other acts deemed necessary or convenient to achieve the 
purposes and objectives of the Alliance. 
6. 
Governing Board:  There is hereby created a Governing Board (also 
referred to as “Board”) to govern the Alliance.  Each Party shall appoint 
one Councilmember or, in the case of the County, one member of the 
Board of Supervisors, to serve on the Governing Board and another 
Councilmember, or Supervisor in the case of the County, to serve as an 
alternate, with each continuing in such capacity until replaced.  The 
Governing Board shall elect one of its members to serve as Chairperson.  
The Board shall meet as needed, but at least one time a year.  Meetings 
shall be held in San Mateo County at a place to be designated.  Each 
member of the Board shall have one vote. 
The Governing Board shall be responsible for establishing the policy 
direction of the Alliance.  On an annual basis, the Board shall adopt a 
work plan and budget for programs, services and subsidies that support the 
Alliance’s purposes.  The Governing Board may from time to time give 
public recognition to Employers and other participants for notable efforts 
and achievements with respect to TDM programs.  The Board shall 
exercise all powers and authority on behalf of the parties and may do any 
and all things necessary to carry out this Agreement.  
7. 
Committees:  The Governing Board shall establish such committees, 
either standing or ad hoc, as it deems necessary and appropriate to assist 
the Alliance in carrying out the purposes of this Agreement.  The 
establishment of standing committees, as well as their composition, 
method of appointment, role and purpose, shall be designated in the 
Bylaws of the Alliance as adopted by the Governing Board.  
8. 
Budget:  The Executive Director annually shall prepare a budget for the 
Alliance setting forth anticipated expenses, financing sources and 
proposed service levels and programs necessary to carry out the purposes 
of this Agreement.  The Executive Director shall recommend the budget to 
the Governing Board for approval after reviewing same with any 
committee the Governing Board may establish and designate for this 
purpose.  In the event the budget contemplates revenue in the form of

monetary contributions from the parties, the budget shall be submitted to 
each Party for approval.  
9. 
Staff of the Alliance:  The Governing Board shall appoint an Executive 
Director.  The Executive Director may hire other staff people for the 
Alliance, as needed, provided that such hiring conforms to the approved 
budget.  The Executive Director may contract for the provision of other 
staff services, provided that such contracts conform to the approved 
budget.  In lieu of an Executive Director, the Governing Board may 
contract for such management services.  Staff or contractors will be 
employee(s) or contractee(s) of the Alliance.  The Executive Director and 
other staff shall serve at the pleasure of the hiring or appointing authority.

work with such committees as may be established and designated for this

(a)

(b) 
Be responsible for day to day personnel matters and for the hiring 
and firing of subordinate staff members; and 
(c) 
Prepare an annual report describing the results of program 
implementation, transportation surveys, TDM programs and other 
information including the successes in attaining the goals and 
objectives to advance the purpose of the Alliance. 
The Governing Board may also appoint legal counsel to represent the 
Alliance. 
10. 
Fiscal Agent:  The member Party designated by resolution of the

Fiscal Agent for the Alliance and shall be charged with the following 
responsibilities: 
(a) 
The custody of all money, property and assets of the Alliance;  
(b) 
The maintenance of all financial books and records necessary to 
conduct the business of the Alliance; and 
(c) 
The development of periodic reports to the Governing Board and 
the Executive Director regarding receipts, disbursements and the 
financial condition of the Alliance.

11. 
Withdrawal:  Any participating Party may withdraw from this Agreement 
by filing written notice of intention to do so with the other parties.  
Termination will take effect on July 1 of any year, provided there is a least 
six months advance notice.  The withdrawal of any Party from this 
Agreement shall in no way affect the rights and obligations of the 
remaining Parties.  If a Party withdraws from this Agreement, it is not 
entitled to return of any funds contributed to the Agency nor to the return 
in cash or in kind of any materials or supplies contributed.  Withdrawing 
Parties still are obligated for all payments due from them for the fiscal 
year of the withdrawal. 
12. 
Termination and Disposition of Property:  This Agreement shall be 
deemed terminated when only one Party continues to participate, or when 
all participating Parties choose to terminate it.  Upon termination, all 
assets shall be distributed in equal shares to the Parties still active at the 
time of termination or to the one Party continuing to participate or to a 
successor agency designated by all of the remaining parties at the time of 
termination, with the exception that if any surplus money of the Alliance 
at the time of termination represents monetary contributions from still 
active member Parties, said money shall be refunded to such Parties in 
proportion to the contributions made. 
13. 
Amendment:  This Agreement may be amended from time to time with 
the written consent of a majority of the participating Parties. 
14. 
Insurance and Indemnification:  The Alliance shall acquire such 
insurance protection, including coverage for workers’ compensation and 
commercial general liability, as is necessary to protect the interests of the 
Governing Board, the Parties, the Alliance staff, representatives, 
volunteers and other participants.  The Alliance shall, at its sole expense, 
assume the defense of and indemnify and save harmless each Party to this 
Agreement and its respective councilmembers, officers, agents and 
employees, from all claims, losses, damages, costs, injury and liability of 
every kind, nature and description directly or indirectly arising from the 
performance of any of the activities, programs or services of the Alliance, 
its Governing Board, or staff. 
15. 
Execution in Counterparts:  This Agreement may be executed in 
counterparts, each of which shall be deemed an original but all of which 
shall constitute one and the same agreement.

SUBJECT:
Poplar Creek Golf Course Pro Shop Concessionaire – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Dana Banke (dba as Golf Super Shop of San Mateo LLC) for an initial term of 7 years to provide 
pro shop concessionaire services at Poplar Creek Golf Course and authorize the Director of Parks and Recreation to 
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented. 
BACKGROUND:
The Golf Super Shop of San Mateo has provided pro shop concessionaire services at Poplar Creek Golf Course since 2008. 
The agreement/management contract with Golf Super Shop of San Mateo was renewed in 2015 for a term of 7 years and 
is set to expire on June 30, 2022. The City has the option to renew this agreement for two additional five-year periods. Per 
the terms of this current agreement, if the City exercises this option the parties will negotiate a new concession agreement 
with terms satisfactory to both parties. It is the desire of the City and Concessionaire to enter into a new agreement for an 
initial term of 7 years with a City renewal option for one 3-year period. 
Over the past 13 years, Dana Banke and his staff have provided excellent customer service and established a positive 
relationship and rapport with all of the guests at Poplar Creek. During his time here, he has expanded the cart fleet, which 
has allowed the golf course to book larger tournaments; provided adult and junior group/private lessons to teach golf and 
grow the game; and he and his staff have been strong supporters of City sponsored programs including the revamped VIP 
program and cloud-based point-of-sale and online reservation system. His working relationship with the maintenance 
staff, Men’s and Women’s golf clubs, and the restaurant concessionaire have all contributed to the overall success of 
Poplar Creek. 
Recently, Poplar Creek has experienced record numbers including over 80,000 rounds played in the last fiscal year, which is 
the largest single year number since 2006. The driving range revenue saw an annual average increase of over 91% since it 
was built in 2014. 
The term of the proposed new concession agreement would commence on the 1st day of July, 2022 and terminate on the 
30th day of June, 2029. It is the desire of the City and Concessionaire to have a fully executed agreement ahead of the June 
30, 2022 termination date in order to secure a new golf cart lease, as the lead time to get new carts has been significantly 
impacted by supply chain issues related to COVID-19.
Other minor modifications to the agreement include:

Changed the threshold of rounds at which time the concessionaire would be eligible to receive an incentive from 
72,000 to 75,000 rounds

Added language regarding expectations for pro shop staff behavior, including professional management of golf tee 
123 of 301

--- page 124 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
sheet and reservations

Changed the threshold for driving range revenue incentive from $450,000 to $250,000 
BUDGET IMPACT:
In exchange for the use of the pro shop, the concessionaire agreement provides for the Golf Super Shop of San Mateo to 
pay the City three percent (3%) of the gross revenues derived from the sale of golf merchandise, power cart and 
equipment rentals, and golf academy/camp fees. The annual revenue from this fee is estimated to be $25,000 to $30,000. 
For the services provided by the Golf Super Shop of San Mateo LLC and its employees, the City will pay a management fee 
of $108,000 per year. The concession agreement also requires that Dana Banke manage the driving range operation 
including labor, equipment, materials, and supplies. The city will reimburse Dana Banke for the cost to operate the driving 
range in an amount not to exceed the annual driving range operating budget of $90,675. Both the management fee and 
driving range operating fee are adjusted annually in accordance with the ALL Urban Consumer Price Index for the San 
Francisco area. 
The City receives all of the revenue from the driving range, golf fees, and membership dues associated with the VIP 
program. The annual revenue from these categories is estimated to be $2,480,500 for fiscal year 2021-22. 
In recognition of the efforts of Dana Banke and his role as an integral part of the success of the golf course, the concession 
agreement provides for several incentive payments to Dana Banke if certain milestones that promote increased use of the 
facility are achieved. For each fiscal year, Dana Banke will receive $3.00 for every paid round of golf above 75,000 rounds, 
twenty-five percent (25%) of driving range revenue above $250,000, fifty percent (50%) of the revenue generated from the 
short game practice area, and forty percent (40%) of the revenue generated from the sale of resident cards.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it relates to the continued operation of the existing golf course 
and does not involve any expansion of the existing use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301).)

All meeting noticing requirements were met.

GOLF COURSE PRO SHOP CONCESSION AGREEMENT  
 
 
 
THIS CONCESSION AGREEMENT, made and entered into this _______________, by 
and between CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation (“CITY”) and  Golf Super Shop 
of San Mateo LLC , a limited liability company .(“CONCESSIONAIRE”). 
 
RECITALS 
 
 
WHEREAS, CITY is the owner of real property consisting of approximately 105 acres 
which includes an 18 hole golf course at 1700 Coyote Point Drive, San Mateo, CA 94401 (the  
“Property”); and 
 
 
WHEREAS, CITY’s property is improved with a parking area, a 3200 SF cart storage 
facility, a Clubhouse Complex, which includes a 1396 SF pro shop, two offices and two storage 
rooms as identified on Exhibit A (the “Premises”); and 
 
 
WHEREAS, CONCESSIONAIRE possesses the skills, experience, ability, background 
and knowledge for the operation of a retail business for the sale and rental of quality golf 
equipment and  merchandise and for the operation of the course pro-shop and related services and 
activities; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, CITY wishes to grant to CONCESSIONAIRE the right to conduct a retail 
sales business and related activities at the Premises as well as golf instruction on the Property upon 
the terms and conditions set forth herein; 
 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration, the parties agree as follows: 
 
Section 1: Terms; Use; Operation 
 
1.1 
Concession.  CITY hereby grants to CONCESSIONAIRE the exclusive right and 
obligation to operate a pro shop on the Premises and to provide golf instruction on the Property 
and the right in common with other users thereof to make use of the parking facilities located 
adjacent to the pro shop. 
 
1.2 
Term. The term of this Agreement shall be for a term of seven years, commencing on the 
1st day of July, 2022, and terminating on the 30th day of June, 2029.  
 
1.3 
Renewal.  If, during the initial term of this Agreement, LESSEE has performed to the City’s 
satisfaction, the CITY shall have the option, to renew this Agreement for one additional three-year 
period.  If the CITY exercises this option, the parties will negotiate a new Concession Agreement 
with terms satisfactory to both parties.  The CITY will inform CONCESSIONAIRE within twelve 
months prior to the expiration of the current term if it intends to renew this Agreement for an 
additional three-year period.   
 
 
1.4 
Use of Premises; Exclusivity.     
 
a. Use of Premises.  CONCESSIONAIRE   may use the Premises for the following uses 
and for no other purpose without CITY’s prior written consent:

• Operation and management of a fully equipped golf shop including the sale 
and rental of quality, recognized name-brand golf equipment. 
 
• Operation and management of the driving range; including group and

• Storage of a minimum of sixty-four (64) powered golf carts for rent to 
golfers.  
 
• Provision of resident identification cards. 
 
b. Exclusivity.  CONCESSIONAIRE shall have the exclusive right to provide golf

Incidental merchandise and equipment may be brought to the course as part of any

the number of events allowed to bring incidental merchandise and equipment onto 
the course exceed four per year.  All such events shall be approved by the Director 
of Parks and Recreation. 
 
1.5 
Operation. 
 
a. Hours of Operation. 
CONCESSIONAIRE  agrees to open the pro shop for 
business every day of the year except Christmas, no later than sunrise and shall remain open 
throughout the day and shall be closed no sooner than dusk.  Any change such as inclement weather 
which shortens the operating hours specified herein shall be subject to prior approval of the Golf 
Services Manager. 
 
b. General method of operation. 
CONCESSIONAIRE shall operate the business on 
the Property continuously during the entire term of this Concession Agreement with such due 
diligence and efficiency as will reasonably produce the maximum return to CONCESSIONAIRE. 
 
c.  Services:  CONCESSIONAIRE shall provide the services and activities typically 
associated with a full-service pro-shop.  These shall include, as a minimum, the following services 
and activities:

regulations.  
 
2) Supervision and control of a starting time system.  
 
3) Collection and daily deposit of green fees.  
 
4) Provision of quality golf lessons and instructions for all levels of play.  
 
5) Promotion of golf and golf related activities in cooperation with existing golf clubs, 
organizations, and CITY.  
 
6) Scheduling and facilitation of golf tournaments, clinics, and junior golf promotions.

Section 2: Payment; Late Payments. 
 
2.1  Payment:  General.  In consideration for CONCESSIONAIRE’s use of the Premises and 
Property provided by CITY, CONCESSIONAIRE shall pay to the CITY for each accounting 
month, the following percentage of gross sales:  
 
Percentage rent will be 3% of the gross sales of pro-shop merchandise sales, power cart 
and equipment rentals, and teaching academies and/or golf camps.  
 
 
Payment will be due quarterly on the 15th day of the month following each fiscal year quarter.  
 
2.2 
Definition of Gross Sales.  “Gross sales” is the sum of all sales at invoice values for Pro 
Shop Merchandise Sales, Power Cart Rentals, other equipment rentals, and teaching academies 
and/or golf camps  As used in this Agreement, the term "Pro-Shop Merchandise Sales" (upon 
which percentage rentals are to be based) shall include the following: the sale price of all goods, 
wares, merchandise and products sold on or from the Pro Shop by CONCESSIONAIRE, his agents 
or any other person acting under contract with CONCESSIONAIRE, whether for cash or credit 
and whether payment is actually made or not; excluding however, fair and reasonable resale and 
employee discount purchases, provided their transactions are made on a cost basis; all sums 
deposited in any coin-operated vending machine or similar device on the Golf Course or in the Pro 
Shop, regardless of the ownership of the machine or device or whether or not such sums are 
removed and counted by CONCESSIONAIRE.  As used in this Agreement, the term "Power Cart 
Rentals" upon which percentage rentals are to be based shall include the rental of power carts, 
whether gas or electric, whether for cash or credit and whether payment is actually made or not.  
 
For purposes of this Agreement, “Gross Sales” shall exclude the following: 
 
(a) All sales taxes and retailers’ excise taxes, paid or collected by, or payable by Operator, 
provided such taxes are added to the selling price and separately stated from the selling 
price of merchandise or services and collected from customers. 
 
(b) Credit Card service charges that are included in the sales price to customers who pay 
by credit or debit card. 
 
(c) Proceeds from the sale of any of CONCESSIONAIRE’s trade fixtures or equipment 
not in the ordinary course of CONCESSIONAIRE’s business.  
 
(d) Redemption of gift certificates at the Premises (provided that CONCESSIONAIRE’s 
revenue from the redemption of gift certificates is included in Gross Sales). 
 
(e) Sale of gift cards and golf shop vouchers at the Premises (provided that 
CONCESSIONAIRE’s revenue from the redemption of gift cards and golf shop 
vouchers is included in Gross Sales) 
 
(f) License or concession fees and other consideration paid to or received from any 
licensee, concessionaire, CONCESSIONAIRE or other operator under concession, 
license or other arrangement for operation of any portion of the facilities.

2.3 
Late Payment.  
 
 
a. CONCESSIONAIRE acknowledges that late payment to CITY of rent or the percentage 
of annual gross sales may cause CITY to incur costs not contemplated by this Concession 
Agreement, the exact amount of such costs being extremely difficult and impracticable to fix.   
 
b. Accordingly, if payment of any sum specified herein due or if any other sum due CITY 
is not received by CITY or postmarked within ten days after the due date, a late charge of one 
percent (1%) of payment due and unpaid plus $25 shall be added to the payment, and the total sum 
shall become immediately due and payable to CITY.  An additional charge of one percent (1%) of 
said payment, excluding late charges, shall be added for each additional month that said payment 
remains unpaid. 
 
c. The parties agree that this late charge represents a fair and reasonable estimate of the 
costs that CITY will incur by reason of the late payment.  Acceptance of any late charge shall not 
constitute a waiver of default with respect to the overdue amount, nor prevent CITY from 
exercising any of its other rights and remedies. 
 
d. If said percentage payments, plus late charges, are not timely paid as outlined above, 
CITY may give CONCESSIONAIRE written notice to make said payments plus late charges, and 
if LESSEE fails to do so within ten days of demand, CITY may, at its option, terminate this 
agreement and CONCESSIONAIRE shall be liable to CITY for all damages suffered by CITY by 
reason of CONCESSIONAIRE’s default and Agreement termination, including, but not limited 
to, all costs and attorney’s fees. 
 
Section 3: Utilities; Maintenance and Repair. 
 
3.1 
Utilities 
 
a. CITY agrees that it will make available to the Premises facilities for the distribution of 
potable water, the removal of sewage, electricity, natural gas, and telephones.   
 
b. CONCESSIONAIRE shall pay for the following utilities: 50% of the utilities metered 
for the building that houses the administrative offices and the pro shop (PG&E), that being the 
portion determined to be assigned to the pro shop operation.  
 
c. CITY shall invoice CONCESSIONAIRE quarterly for those utilities not specifically 
billed to him.  Utilities shall be: gas and electricity.  Payments for utilities shall be due 30 days 
from the date of invoice.  Delinquent payments shall be subject to 10% penalty plus 1.5% interest 
per month.  
 
d. CITY shall provide, maintain and pay for the costs of the building security system; 
except that all false alarm charges resulting from the misuse of the alarm system by 
CONCESSIONAIRE, including employees, shall be the responsibility of CONCESSIONAIRE.

walkways and public restroom areas; exterior of the Clubhouse structure and support systems not

Shop.

thereof, including but not limited to the cost of labor, materials and equipment and a 15% charge

a statement of said cost from CITY representative.

supplies, including but not limited to interior light bulbs and paper products and to provide, repair 
and maintain all CITY approved signs used in conjunction with the pro shop operation. CITY will

improvements to the interior of the Premises, except as set forth below. CONCESSIONAIRE 
hereby waives all right to make repairs at the expense of CITY.  All such repairs and/or 
modifications or additions of a permanent nature to the facilities shall have approval, in writing, 
by CITY prior to implementation by CONCESSIONAIRE.

any part of any portion of the building, grounds or equipment belonging to CITY or to add interior 
decorations, including signs, without first securing the consent of CITY in writing.  Any approved 
changes to the buildings or grounds, which are built-in and permanently affixed to the structure,

CONCESSIONAIRE, including claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense caused or claimed to

volunteers. CONCESSIONAIRE agrees to defend CITY, its elected and appointed officials,  
employees, agents, and volunteers against any such claims.  This provision does not apply to 
claims, loss, liability or damage or expense arising from the sole negligence, willful misconduct, 
or active negligence of CITY.

Section 5: Records; Taxes; Permits; Licenses; Other Financial Responsibilities. 
 
5.1 
Records and Accounting. 
 
 
a. All fees, gross revenues and other monies collected by CONCESSIONAIRE shall be 
processed through the point of sale system provided by the CITY and in the manner prescribed by 
the CITY.  All green fees shall belong to the CITY and shall be deposited in accordance with the 
policies and procedures as defined by the City Finance Director's office.  CONCESSIONAIRE 
shall submit a daily report of the amounts collected for revenues due to the City of San Mateo and 
to CONCESSIONAIRE.  The CITY will verify accuracy of the daily report and perform daily 
reconciliation of all revenue and non-revenue payments collected through the golf course point of 
sale. CONCESSIONAIRE shall hold in a fiduciary capacity and not make any private or other 
unauthorized use of fees or the portions of gross revenues required to be paid by 
CONCESSIONAIRE to the CITY. CONCESSIONAIRE shall insure that daily bank deposits are 
accurate with no more than a 2% error rate per month when compared against bank reconciliations.  
CONCESSIONAIRE shall be responsible for any shortages in monies collected on behalf of and 
required to be paid to CITY. 
 
b. CONCESSIONAIRE shall, at all times during the term of this Agreement, keep or cause 
to be kept, true and complete records and accounts of all financial transactions conducted in the 
operation of all business activities.  The records must be supported by source documents such as 
sales slips, cash register tapes, purchase invoices or other pertinent documents.  Except as may be 
otherwise provided in this Agreement, all retail sales and charges shall be recorded by means of 
cash registers or other comparable devices which display the amount of the transaction and 
automatically issue a receipt.  Totals registered shall be read and recorded at the end of each day 
and shall be individually recorded.  CONCESSIONAIRE shall permit the CITY through its 
designated representatives to inspect such accounts and all other records at any time upon demand.  
 
c.  CITY shall be allowed to inspect and audit the books of accounts and records and any 
supporting source documents at any and all reasonable times during the term of this Agreement.  
 
5.2 
Taxes. CONCESSIONAIRE shall pay, when due, all taxes and assessments levied upon 
the Premises and personal property situated in the Premises. CONCESSIONAIRE is not required 
to pay personal property taxes for property owned by CITY. 
 
5.3   Payment of Any Possessory Interest Taxes Levied by County.  CONCESSIONAIRE 
recognizes and understands that, in the event that the County of San Mateo interprets this 
Agreement to create a real property possessory interests subject to the County’s possessory interest 
tax, CONCESSIONAIRE is responsible for payment of those taxes. 
 
 
 
 
 
5.4 
Permits and Licenses.  CONCESSIONAIRE shall procure all permits and licenses and pay 
all charges and fees incidental to the lawful conduct of the services, and keep fully informed on all 
existing future Federal, State and local laws, ordinances, and regulations which in any manner 
affect the fulfillment of this agreement.

Section 6: Golf Operations. 
 
6.1 
Starters and Assistants. 
 
a. CONCESSIONAIRE shall be responsible for hiring, training and supervising qualified, 
competent and experienced personnel who will represent CONCESSIONAIRE and act on its 
behalf.  CONCESSIONAIRE shall require its attendants and employees to be neatly attired in 
clean and appropriate uniforms, courteous, and efficient at all times. CONCESSIONAIRE shall 
maintain supervision over attendants and employees to insure the maintenance of a high standard 
of service and courtesy to the public.  Failure to maintain a high standard of service and courtesy 
may be reason to terminate this agreement.  
 
            b. CONCESSIONAIRE shall employ a full-time PGA Golf Professional to supervise and 
control all golf operations. 
 
 
c. A minimum of one full-time Golf Professional Assistant shall be hired to assist with 
teaching and general pro shop operations.  Said employee(s) shall generally, meet the 
qualifications as a PGA Apprentice Professional.  A sufficient number of starters shall be 
employed to ensure that the Pro Shop is staffed with a minimum of two staff members at all times 
and to provide quality reservation and merchandising assistance to the public.   
 
d. All compensation of starters and assistants shall be paid by CONCESSIONAIRE; such 
starters and assistants shall be his employees and not employees or agents of the CITY.  CITY 
shall not be responsible for payment of any compensation to starters or assistants.  
 
e.   CONCESSIONAIRE shall ensure that all starters and assistants manage the electronic 
tee sheet according to the standards set forth by the CITY, including, but not limited to: 1). 
Reserving tee times for specific booking groups no more than the maximum number of days in 
advance that the said group is allowed to book; 2). Charging the appropriate green fee for each 
booking group with no unauthorized discounts; 3). Not providing preferential or reoccurring tee 
times to any group.    
 
6.2  
Golf Carts.  CONCESSIONAIRE shall provide no less than 64 power rental carts that will 
be available for public rent. Carts shall be clean and maintained in a manner that is presentable to 
the public. A comprehensive maintenance program shall be instituted to ensure that vehicles for 
rent are safe and in good working order.  
 
CONCESSIONAIRE shall provide an adequate number of handcarts that will be available for 
public rent and will ensure that the carts are reasonably clean and in good working order.  
 
6.3 
Resident Cards.  
 
a. CITY shall set the fee for Resident Cards and all resident card fees belong to the 
CITY.  
 
b. CONCESSIONAIRE shall issue Resident Cards to those persons that provide 
acceptable proof of residency in the City of San Mateo as specified by the CITY.  
CONCESSIONAIRE shall maintain and update the database containing Resident Card Holders.  
In return for these services the CITY shall pay CONCESSIONAIRE 40% of the revenue derived 
from the sale of Resident Cards.

6.4 
Golf Rangers.   CONCESSIONAIRE shall recruit, train, schedule and supervise a staff of 
volunteer golf rangers.  Rangers shall be available and scheduled daily during peak play periods. 
CONCESSIONAIRE shall provide a written job description, schedule monthly staff meetings, and 
develop and administer a written training program. Volunteer golf rangers shall be enrolled in the 
City’s volunteer program. Volunteer golf rangers may be eligible for golf playing privileges as 
specified by the Golf Services Manager. 
 
6.5 
Lessons. CONCESSIONAIRE shall be responsible for hiring, training and supervising 
qualified, competent and experienced personnel and instructors to develop, teach and administer a 
comprehensive lesson program that includes the following:  
 
(a) 
Community group lesson program.  
 
(b) 
Private and semi-private lessons with optional video instruction.  
 
(c) 
Free or low cost clinics such as rules, etiquette and/or swing improvement clinics that 
will enhance public enjoyment of golf.  
 
6.6 
Programs, Club Activities, Tournaments. CONCESSIONAIRE shall provide services, 
activities and programs to golfers that promote enjoyment, growth and involvement in the game 
including the following:  
 
(a) Programs. CONCESSIONAIRE shall outline a strategy for establishing a Junior Golf 
Program that includes the following elements: collaboration with schools, the Park and 
Recreation Department and other youth serving organizations; potential for Poplar 
Creek to become an affiliate of The First Tee Program; free or low cost clinics and 
classes; junior golf training academy and/or junior golf camps; and, the expansion and 
enhancement of the Jr. O'Brien Tournament. CONCESSIONAIRE shall explore the 
need and provide recommendations on possible new club organizations such as 
business leagues, twilight leagues, working women leagues, Footgolf leagues, etc. that 
will stimulate a broader base of play.  
 
CONCESSIONAIRE shall be responsible for hiring, training and supervising qualified, 
competent and experienced personnel and instructors to teach and administer the junior 
golf programs.  
 
b) Club Affiliations. CONCESSIONAIRE shall work with existing resident golf clubs to 
explore opportunities for enhancing and promoting their activities and attend meetings 
on a regular basis to insure on-going communication.  
 
c) Tournaments. CONCESSIONAIRE shall be responsible for hiring, training and 
supervising qualified, competent and experienced personnel to coordinate, plan and 
schedule group tournament activities that minimize conflict with normal daily play 
while increasing play potential. CONCESSIONAIRE shall prepare and market 
tournament services that may include any or all of the following services:  
1) Pairings and starting assignments  
2) Format and distribution of rule sheets  
3) Scorecard collection; score posting and recording 
4) Results reporting  
5) Cart assignments  
6) Merchandise and/or gift certificates package

6.7 
Promoting Increased Play/Marketing.   
 
a. CONCESSIONAIRE shall: 
(1) develop and implement procedures, programs, and promotions to increase play

(2) be responsible for the development and execution of the overall marketing plan

(3)  provide continuous updates to the golf course website to keep the content fresh

(4) be responsible for hiring, training, and supervising qualified and competent

calendar of weekly topics, events and programs to be promoted, and a schedule 
showing the frequency and type of communication contacts.  These contacts 
should include email blasts to the golf course database, push notifications to the 
users that have downloaded the Poplar Creek mobile application, and postings 
to social media sites, such as Facebook, Twitter and Instagram. 
 
b.  CITY shall pay CONCESSIONAIRE a fee of $3 for each paid round in excess of 75,000 
paid annual rounds.  The total earned fees, if any, will be paid as a lump sum at the conclusion of 
each twelve-month period following the commencement of this Agreement. 
 
6.8 
Driving Range & Paid Practice Area

(2) be responsible for the collection, cleaning, and rental of driving range golf balls.  
Pricing for the rental of driving range golf balls will be set by the CITY. 
 
(3) be responsible for the daily maintenance and cleaning of the tee area and hitting 
stalls, equipment building, cart storage area, and trash receptacles and keeping all 
equipment and supplies in good repair. 
 
(4) provide an annual operating budget for the driving range to the Golf Services 
Manager for approval each year. The budget will cover all costs for operating the 
driving range including labor, equipment, materials and supplies.

(5) utilize staff to monitor use of the paid practice area to ensure that those players

6.9 
Prohibitions. CONCESSIONAIRE, its agents and employees, shall not do any of the 
following acts, except as herein otherwise provided and with the written consent of the CITY:  
 
a. Permit any persons to play on the golf course without charge or issue any passes, unless 
the City Manager or his designee, shall have authorized him in writing to do so. 
 
b. Have any material financial or other interest in the control, operation or promotion of 
any other golf course or golf equipment merchandising business within 10 miles from the Poplar 
Creek Golf Course, it being the intent of the CITY that the management and operation of the Pro 
Shop shall be the sole and full-time golf business enterprise conducted by CONCESSIONAIRE 
within the immediate area;  
 
c. Become an officer or member of any golf club or organization of golfers formed or to 
be formed at the Golf Course or in any organization in which participation would conflict with the 
orderly and efficient operation of the Pro Shop and particularly in the granting of starting time or 
other playing privileges;  
 
d. Grant any preferential treatment to any individual or group of individuals including, but 
not limited to, granting of starting time or playing privileges, except as authorized in the rules and 
regulations adopted by the City Council.  
 
e. Attach, hang or otherwise affix any sign or advertising matter on the exterior of the Pro 
Shop.  
  
f. Permit vendors to display or sell goods, wares, merchandise or services either within 
the interior or exterior of the Pro Shop or anywhere on the golf course.  
 
g.  Attempt to bind the CITY to any contracts or other obligations of any nature.

services outlined in Section 6: Golf Operations. In July of each subsequent year this amount shall

CONCESSIONAIRE , other than described in subparagraph (b) above, where such

required for its cure, then CONCESSIONAIRE  shall not be deemed to be in default if

creditors,

8.1

Subordination.  This Agreement shall at all times be subordinated to the lien of any

b. This provision for subordination is self-operative and no further instrument of 
subordination is necessary.  Nevertheless, in confirmation of such subordination, 
CONCESSIONAIRE shall execute promptly any instruments that CITY may

submitted to mediation. The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request. The

submit one name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the 
California State Board of Mediation and Conciliation, or other agreed–upon service. The mediator 
shall be selected by a "blindfolded" process. 
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties. Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party. No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement. The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but

Exhibit A – Insurance Requirements 
 
 
 
Concessionaire shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract insurance against 
claims for injuries to persons or damages to property which may arise from or in connection with 
the Concessionaire operation and use of the leased premises.  The cost of such insurance shall be 
borne by the Concessionaire. 
 
 
Minimum Scope of Insurance 
 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
 
1.  Insurance Services Office Commercial General Liability coverage  
 
(occurrence form CG 0001). 
 
2. Workers’ Compensation insurance as required by the State California 
 
and Employer’s Liability insurance. 
 
3. Property insurance against all risks of loss to any tenant improvements 
 
or betterments. 
 
 
Minimum Limits of Insurance 
 
Concessionaire shall maintain limits no less than: 
 
1.  General liability:  $2,000,000 per occurrence for bodily injury, personal injury and property 
damage.  If Commercial General Liability Insurance or other form with a general aggregate 
limit is used, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location 
or the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
 
2. Employer’s Liability: 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury or disease. 
 
3. Property Insurance: 
Full replacement cost with no coinsurance penalty provision. 
 
 
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions 
 
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City.  At the 
option of the City, either:  the insurer shall reduce or eliminate such deductibles or self-insured 
retentions as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees and agents; or 
Concessionaire shall provide a financial guarantee satisfactory to City guaranteeing payment of 
losses and related investigations, claim administration and defense expenses. 
 
 
Other Insurance Provisions 
 
The general liability policy is to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
 
DocuSign Envelope ID: 7B50DDB9-0DC8-4133-B384-E83B33A601B7

1. The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees and agents are to be covered as 
insureds with respect to liability arising out of use of City’s property. 
 
2. Concessionaire’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance as respects the City, its  
elected and appointed officials, employees and agents.  Any insurance or self-insurance 
maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees or agents shall be excess 
of Concessionaire’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
 
3. Each insurance policy required by this clause shall be endorsed to state that coverage  
shall not be canceled, except after thirty (30) day’s prior written notice has been provided to 
the City. 
 
 
Acceptability of Insurers 
 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VI, 
unless otherwise acceptable by City. 
 
 
Verification of Coverage 
 
Concessionaire shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements 
effecting coverage required by this clause.  The endorsements should be on forms provided by the 
City or on other than the City’s forms, provided those endorsements or policies conform to the 
requirements.  All certificates and endorsements are to be received and approved by the City 
before work commences.  However, failure to do so shall not operate as a waiver of these 
insurance requirements.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements effecting the coverage required by these 
specifications at any time.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  13
Section Name: PUBLIC HEARING
File ID: 21-5370
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
City Clerk's Office
MEETING DATE:
November 01, 2021 
SUBJECT:
Ordinance Introduction – Transition to District-Based Elections for Council Members – Public Hearing #5
RECOMMENDATION:
Introduce an Ordinance to amend the San Mateo Municipal Code to add Chapter 2.05 "City Council District Elections" to 
establish five council districts, approve the map identifying district boundaries, set the first by-district elections for three 
districts for November 2022 and two districts for November 2024, and provide final direction on the sequence of district 
elections. 
BACKGROUND:
This represents the last of five public hearings required by State law before adopting an ordinance approving a transition 
from at-large elections to by-district elections.  The proposed ordinance provides for the election of members of the City 
Council by five districts, establishes the boundaries and identification number of each district, establishes the election 
order of each district, and adds Chapter 2.05, “City Council District Elections” to Title 2 of the San Mateo Municipal Code.  
The ordinance has been drafted to be consistent with the California Voting Rights Act (CVRA), other pertinent State law 
(such as Elections Code Section 10010 and Government Code Sections 34871 and 34886), as well as the California 
Constitution and the City Charter.  
As drafted, the ordinance would also allow the City Clerk to make technical adjustments to district boundaries that do not 
substantively affect the populations in the districts, the eligibility of candidates, or the residence of elected officials within 
any district.  Provided however, the City Clerk must consult with the City Manager and City Attorney as to the need for any 
such adjustments and must inform the City Council.  The City Clerk is to also direct the City’s demographer to obtain a 
metes-and-bounds description of each district, which is to be submitted to the City Council at its next regular meeting and 
kept on file with the City Clerk’s office for public review.  
Consistent with the schedule adopted by the City Council, the proposed ordinance is scheduled for adoption at the regular 
meeting of November 15, 2021, if the Council introduces the ordinance this evening.  
The City Council held the first and second public hearings prior to any draft maps being drawn on August 23 and 
September 13. In these hearings Council reviewed the composition and number of districts, form of government under 
consideration, charter amendment considerations, and the public input process. At its September 13 hearing, the Council 
provided direction to begin drawing draft maps for a by-district election system comprised of five districts and a rotational 
mayor.
In accordance with Elections Code 10010, the City held two more public hearings to review draft maps submitted by its 
demographer on September 30 and October 14. The City received numerous comments and additional submittals of 
suggested map lines as part of this public process. At the October 14 hearing, the Council was presented with two 
145 of 301

--- page 146 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
variations of draft map No. 3, presented as map 3b and map 3c, and Council, after much public input and deliberation 
settled on map 3b, which is now considered the Final Draft Map. Discussion ensued on the process of sequencing the 
districts, with final direction to be given at this public hearing. 
Next Steps 
Council must include the sequencing of district elections as part of the ordinance. Map 3b was originally presented with 
random alpha designations for the five proposed districts. Staff is proposing using numbers for the districts in the following 
manner: 
C = 1
E = 2
D = 3
A = 4 or 5
B = 4 or 5
Staff also proposes using odd numbers for the three districts that would elect Councilmembers in November 2022, and 
even numbers for the remaining two districts up for election in November 2024. At the October 14, 2021 meeting, it was 
suggested that Districts C and D could be set for the November 2022 election, and District E for the November 2024 
election.  Accordingly, the last district that Council selects for the November 2022 election (either District A or District B) 
would be numbered as District 5, and the remaining district would become District 4.  Council is being asked to consider 
the proposed sequencing and to provide final direction on the sequencing order.  
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact from this administrative action.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
Adoption of this ordinance is exempt from environmental review as it does not qualify as a “project” pursuant to the 
California Environmental Quality Act (“CEQA”), under Public Resource Code Section 21065 and CEQA Guidelines Sections 
15061(b)(3), 15320, and 15378, as there is no possibility that such action would cause either a direct, or reasonably 
foreseeable indirect, physical change in the environment. 
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
DRAFT ORDINANCE 
Providing for the Election of Members of the City Council by Five Districts, Establishing the Boundaries and 
Identification Number of Each District, Establishing  the Election Order of Each District, and Adding Chapter 
2.05 “City Council District Elections” to Title 2 of the San Mateo Municipal Code 
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo uses an at-large method of election which is consistent with the 
guarantees of Section 7 of Article 1 and of Section 2 of Article II of the California Constitution; and 
WHEREAS, California Government Code Section 34886 permits the City Council to change the method of 
election by ordinance to a “by-district” system in which each member of the City Council is elected only by the 
voters in the district in which the candidate resides, in accordance with California Government Code Section 
34871; and 
WHEREAS, a by-district system can also be consistent with the guarantees of Section 7 of Article 1 and of 
Section 2 of Article II of the California Constitution; and 
WHEREAS, under the provisions of California Elections Code Section 10010, a city that changes from an 
at-large city council method of election to a by-district city council method of election must hold a total of five 
public hearings, which includes at least two public hearings regarding potential voting district boundaries prior 
to the release and consideration of any draft voting district maps, and two public hearings following the release 
of draft voting district maps; and 
WHEREAS, on June 21, 2021, the City Council adopted Resolution No. 69 (2021) that initiated the 
process of establishing a by-district election system and adopted a public hearing schedule; and 
WHEREAS, on July 19, 2021, the City Council adopted Resolution No. 76 (2021) that approved a revised 
public hearing schedule in order to use updated 2020 Census data; and 
WHEREAS, on August 23, 2021 and September 13, 2021, pursuant to California Elections Code Section 
10010(a)(1), the City Council held public hearings where the public was invited to provide input regarding the 
composition of the City’s voting districts before any draft maps were drawn, and the City Council of the City of 
San Mateo considered and discussed the same; and 
WHEREAS, on September 30, 2021 and October 14, 2021 pursuant to California Elections Code Section 
10010(a)(2), the City Council held public hearings where the public was invited to provide input regarding the 
content of the draft maps that had been released and published at least seven (7) days before each meeting, 
and the proposed sequence of elections, and the City Council of the City of San Mateo considered and discussed 
the same; and  
WHEREAS, at its meeting on October 14, 2021, the City Council directed staff to prepare an ordinance 
adopting a voting district map for the City Council’s consideration; and  
WHEREAS, on November 1, 2021, the City Council held a final public hearing on the proposal to establish 
district boundaries, reviewed additional public input, formally selected the voting district map and the election 
147 of 301

--- page 148 ---
sequence attached to, incorporated in, and set forth, in this ordinance as Exhibit A, which was introduced for a 
first reading at the same regular meeting; and 
WHEREAS, throughout the foregoing process, the City engaged in a significant amount of public 
outreach and engagement above and beyond the public hearings and other procedures required by California 
Elections Code Section 10010, including, but not limited to, community forums; and  
WHEREAS, the purpose of this ordinance is to enact, pursuant to California Government Code Section 
34886, an ordinance providing for the election of members of the City Council of the City of San Mateo by 
district in five single-member districts as reflected in the voting district map referred to as Map 3b and attached 
as Exhibit A to this ordinance, in furtherance of the purposes of the California Voting Rights Act of 2001 (Chapter 
1.5 (commencing with Section 14025) of Division 14 of the Elections Code) to encourage by-district elections as 
one method to implement the guarantees of Section 7 of Article 1 and of Section 2 of Article II of the California 
Constitution. 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS: 
Section 1. Chapter 2.05 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Title 2 as follows: 
Chapter 2.05 
City Council District Elections 
2.05.010 Declaration of Purpose. 
The City Council hereby declares that the purpose of this ordinance is to change the method of electing 
members of this Council to a by-district method as defined in the California Voting Rights Act of 2001. 
2.05.020 City Council Districts Established. 
Five City Council districts are hereby established in the City of San Mateo. The boundaries and 
identifying number of each district shall be as described on the Council District Map as shown below. 
[District Map attached hereto as Exhibit A and incorporated herein to be published in the Municipal 
Code]  
2.05.030. Election of Members of the City Council by-District. 
(a) Following the effective date of this ordinance and upon the commencement of “by-district” elections 
in the order established in Section 2.05.040 of this Code, members of the City Council shall be elected “by 
district” as defined in California Government Code Section 34871 or any successor statute.  Any candidate for 
City Council must have been a resident and elector of the district in which he or she seeks election for at least 
thirty days before the time he or she files nominating papers or equivalent declaration of candidacy for such 
office, or such person’s appointment to fill a vacancy therein. No term of any member of the City Council that 
commenced prior to the effective date of this ordinance shall be affected by the adoption of this ordinance. A 
vacancy in an office filled by at-large election shall be filled by appointment or election from the City at-large in 
accordance with the Charter. 
148 of 301

--- page 149 ---
(b) Registered voters signing nomination papers or voting for a member of the City Council shall be 
residents of the geographical area making up the district from which the member is to be elected. 
(c) The terms of the office of each member elected to the City Council shall remain four (4) years. 
2.05.040 Commencement of District Elections.  
(a) Commencing on the general municipal election in 2022 and every four years thereafter the voters in 
districts __, __, and __, shall elect members of the City Council by district for full four (4) year terms. At the 
general municipal election in 2024 and every four years thereafter, the voters in districts __, and __ shall elect 
members of the City Council by district for full four (4) year terms. 
(b) The term of office of any council member who has been elected and whose term of office has not 
expired shall not be affected by any change in the boundaries of the district from which he or she was elected. 
Section 2. Technical Adjustments and Metes-and-Bounds.  
If necessary to facilitate the implementation of this ordinance, the City Clerk is authorized to make 
technical adjustments to the district boundaries that do not substantively affect the populations in the districts, 
the eligibility of candidates, or the residence of elected officials within any district.  The City Clerk shall consult 
with the City Manager and City Attorney concerning any technical adjustments deemed necessary and shall 
advise the City Council of any such adjustments required in the implementation of the districts. The City Clerk 
shall also direct the City’s demographer to provide a metes-and-bounds description of each district as shown on 
the map attached as Exhibit A and incorporated herein by reference, which shall be submitted to the City 
Council at its next regular meeting and kept on file in the City Clerk’s office for public review. 
Section 3. Environmental Determination. Adoption of this ordinance is exempt from environmental review as 
the adoption of this ordinance does not qualify as a “project” pursuant to the California Environmental Quality 
Act (“CEQA”), under Public Resource Code Section 21065 and CEQA Guidelines Sections 15061(b)(3), 15320, and 
15378, as there is no possibility that such action would cause either a direct, or reasonably foreseeable indirect, 
physical change in the environment. 
Section 4. Severability. In the event any section, clause or provision of this ordinance shall be determined 
invalid or unconstitutional, such section, clause or provision shall be deemed severable and all other sections or 
portions hereof shall remain in full force and effect. 
Section 5. Publication. This ordinance shall be published in summary in a newspaper of general circulation, 
posted in the City Clerk's Office, and posted on the City's website, all in accord with Section 2.15 of the City 
Charter. 
Section 6. Legislative History and Effective Date. This ordinance was introduced on Clerk to complete., and 
adopted on Clerk to complete., and shall be effective 30 days after its adoption.

process.

From: North Shoreview <nsna.sanmateo@gmail.com>  
Sent: Thursday, October 14, 2021 1:56 PM 
To: Eric Rodriguez <erodriguez@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Council (San Mateo) 
<CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: Districting Effort and North Shoreview Neighborhood 
 
Dear Mayor Rodriguez and City Council Members, 
 
We first of all wanted to thank Mayor Eric Rodriguez for meeting with our neighborhood association last 
Sunday via zoom. As we discussed during that meeting we are hopeful that a district map can be found 
that does not split our North Shoreview neighborhood. We would like to stay together and we also think 
it is important that we are in the same district with the other shoreline neighborhoods and we share 
very serious issues and are a geographical unity and communities of interest such as the flood zones, sea 
water riise, as well as the bay trail and parks..  
 
We hope that the demographers were able to look at the map submitted by SMUHA President Michael 
Nash. We looked at it and felt that it met the needed qualifications.  
 
Here is a link to the map proposed and submitted by Michael Nash:   
https://districtr.org/edit/61566?event=san_mateo_city 
 
Please let us know what else can be done in the hopes of not splitting our neighborhood and keeping 
the shoreline east side of San Mateo in one district. 
 
 
Thank you, 
 
--  
Cynthia Newton 
President, North Shoreview Neighborhood Association

--- page 169 ---
From: Vincenza Sebastiani <  
Sent: Thursday, October 14, 2021 3:59 PM 
To: District Elections <districtelections@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Cc: Victor Marino < >; Enza Sebastiani < > 
Subject: Overall safety in San Mateo, CA 
 
Hi, among many topics, we would like to address the following: 
 
1. Overall safety: the pandemic didn’t help making us feeling safe around our neighborhood. Ring and 
security cameras on a daily basis are capturing trespassers, aware of such devices, but carelessly steeling 
packages, tools, mail, breaking into cars and simply disregarding other people properties.  
 
2. COVID-19 Vaccination status: seriously appalled at the fact that no business nor government office is 
asking for a green pass or a vaccination status when entering indoor spaces, offices, hospitals, etc. 
 
4. Streets, train stations and upper/underpass cleanliness: the need for deep cleaning of streets, 
garages, parking lots, stations, and upper/underpasses cannot be stressed more, particularly now, while 
we are still trying to end the COVID-19 pandemic. 
 
5. Homeless: are there any plans to increase and properly manage the yearly budget to end 
homelessness and address mental health in the homeless population? It saddens us to see that so many 
people in need are left on the streets without meds to control their anger and mental diseases. 
 
6. Parking and properly marked sidewalks at intersections: there are multiple intersections in our 
neighborhood that are unsafe to use. Quite a few accidents caused bikers to be rushed to ER as well as 
drivers. If sidewalks would be properly marked, we wouldn’t see SUV and Truck the size of a boat parked 
right at the corner of intersections which become death traps for drivers, pedestrians and bikers. Worst 
intersection is N. Norfolk and Dore, Huron Avenue and Trollman, the list goes on. 
 
7. Incentivize new business in downtown San Mateo: while landlords prefer to keep their doors shut 
until they find new business owners willing to pay one year salary x one month worth of rent, San Mateo 
is losing money and charm and the possibility of hosting not only restaurants and cafes but also a variety 
of stores that could really attract a growing multicultural population. For example, during the course of 
two decades, only one book store opened their doors in San Mateo. 
 
8. Public water fountains: It would really help reducing plastic consumption and pollution, improving 
the overall downtown look. 
 
Thanks for Reading, 
 
Enza Sebastiani and Victor Marino.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  14
Section Name: PUBLIC HEARING
File ID: 21-5298
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Community Development
MEETING DATE:
November 1, 2021 
SUBJECT:
Ordinance Introduction and Resolution Adoption – Impact and In-Lieu Fee Updates
RECOMMENDATIONS:
1.
Introduce an Ordinance to (a) amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapters 27.13, “Transportation Improvement 
Fee,” and 23.60, “Art in Public Places,” (b) rescind Sections 03.54.060, “Sewer Connection Charges,” and 3.54.080, 
“South Trunk Sewer Area Impact Fee,” and (c) add Section 7.38.065, “Wastewater Capacity Charge,” and Chapter 
23.65, “Childcare Impact Fee;” and 
2.
Adopt a Resolution to (a) establish a Wastewater Capacity Charge, (b) update the Art in Public Places In Lieu Fee, 
(c) update the Childcare Development Impact Fee, (d) update the Transportation Improvement Fee, and (e) 
rescind Resolutions No. 34 (2004) and 88 (2005) relating to the previously-imposed Childcare Development Impact 
Fee. 
BACKGROUND:
In fiscal year 2019-20, the San Mateo City Council included a review of the City’s development impact fees as a priority in 
its strategic plan. As a result, in 2020, the City entered into a contract with two consultants, Matrix Consulting Group and 
Bartle Wells, to review several of the City’s development impact and in-lieu fees (Table 1).

On June 7, 2021, staff presented the findings of the two nexus studies to City Council, seeking guidance on proposed 
173 of 301

--- page 174 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
structural changes, potential fee subsidies, and the timeline for implementation, including the treatment of planning 
applications already in the development pipeline. Based on City Council direction in that June meeting, staff is returning to 
Council with updates to several of the City’s impact and in-lieu fees, including amendments to the San Mateo Municipal 
Code (SMMC) outlined in the proposed Ordinance (Attachment 1) and a proposed Resolution (Attachment 2) to establish 
the new fee amounts and structures.
Purpose of Studies and Key Findings
Development impact fees are governed by Government Code Sections 66000 et seq., also known as “AB 1600,” which 
specify the need for a nexus between the collection of fees and new development within a city’s service area. The nexus 
studies (Exhibits A and B to the proposed Resolution) outline the maximum allowable fees the City would be justified in 
charging based on projected future growth, the infrastructure costs the City will incur to accommodate that growth, and 
the City’s legal requirements under AB 1600. 
The City continues to have the legal authority to charge all its current impact and in-lieu fees, but the nexus studies 
indicate that apart from the Childcare Impact Fee, the current rates across all fee types are below the full costs the City will 
incur to accommodate projected future growth. In addition, changes to legal parameters, infrastructure costs, or the nexus 
determinations themselves have led to structural changes to several of the City’s fees. This section outlines the major 
findings from the two studies and the specific changes to the SMMC included in the proposed Ordinance.
Transportation Improvement Fee
The Transportation Improvement Fee was last updated in 2017 and allows the City to charge new developments to 
mitigate their impact on the City’s transportation network. This fee is assessed on both residential and commercial 
projects, and subsequent revenue can be used to fund a number of transportation-related improvements. The 
Transportation Improvement Fee was included in this study to allow Public Works to include updated cost estimates and 
project listings for future infrastructure improvements. 
Based on the Matrix nexus study, the City is currently under-recovering for all Transportation Improvement Fee categories. 
In addition, while the City currently charges only industrial, retail, and office uses within the commercial category, a nexus 
exists to also charge hotels and institutions. While “hotel” is already defined in Chapter 27.13 of the SMMC, the proposed 
Ordinance amends Section 27.13.040 to add a definition for “institutions” as well. “Institution” uses include government 
buildings, schools, and museums. The proposed Ordinance also makes additional changes to Chapter 27.13 to streamline 
the list of land use definitions to include only those explicitly listed in the City’s comprehensive study for the 
Transportation Improvement Fee. The proposed Resolution establishes the updated Transportation Improvement Fee 
amounts by land use.
Childcare Impact Fee
Adopted by Resolutions No. 34 (2004) and 88 (2005), the Childcare Impact Fee allows the City to charge a fee to 
commercial projects greater than 10,000 square feet to account for future childcare needs driven by that development. 
The City can utilize revenue generated from this fee to fund the construction and expansion of future and existing 
childcare facilities. Based on projected future childcare needs and updated construction costs, the nexus study indicated 
the City must reduce the per square foot fee for all commercial uses but could also opt to eliminate the 10,000 square foot 
requirement, meaning the fee would be levied on all commercial uses, regardless of size. In addition, the study established 
a clear nexus between future residential growth and the need for childcare, allowing the City to charge single and multi-
family units a proportionate amount to account for future childcare demand driven by those development types.
Based on Council direction, the proposed Resolution amends the Childcare Impact Fee to eliminate the 10,000 square foot 
requirement for commercial developments and impose the fee on new residential developments. In addition, the 
proposed Resolution rescinds Resolutions No. 34 (2004) and 88 (2005), and the proposed Ordinance adds Chapter 23.65 to 
the SMMC, codifying the fee for ease of reference. 
Wastewater Capacity Charge
The City currently has three sets of sewer fees that are applied to new developments to mitigate their impacts on the 
174 of 301

--- page 175 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
sewer system infrastructure. These include the sewer connection fees, the Wastewater Treatment Plant Phase II Expansion 
Fee and the South Trunk Area Sewer Improvement fees, which are only levied on new developments located in the area 
served by the City’s South Trunk sewer line. Staff last updated the sewer fees in 2014, with an update to the South Trunk 
Area Sewer Improvement fee.
City staff hired Bartle Wells to review the sewer development fees because of its specific experience developing water and 
wastewater fees. Following its review, Bartle Wells recommended that staff adopt a single set of wastewater capacity 
charges that would be applied uniformly throughout the City. Section 66013 of the Government Code specifically governs 
water and wastewater capacity charges and defines a “capacity charge” to mean “a charge for public facilities in existence 
at the time a charge is imposed or charges for new public facilities to be acquired or constructed in the future that are of 
proportional benefit to the person or property being charged.” The new capacity charges will replace all three existing 
development fees.
Bartle Wells developed the proposed capacity charges using an average cost approach in which new developments pay for 
their proportionate share of the average cost of facilities, both existing and planned, needed to meet the demands of the 
City’s service area. As part of this approach, the report recommended that redevelopment projects continue to receive a 
credit for their existing sewer connections and only pay for the incremental demand generated by new development. 
About 90% of the revenues collected from the proposed wastewater capacity charges can be used to fund capital 
improvements for wastewater repair, rehabilitation, and replacement. The remaining revenues are eligible to fund capital 
improvements that represent upgrades and expansions to the City’s sewer system infrastructure.
Based on Council direction, the proposed Ordinance repeals Sections 03.54.060, “Sewer Connection Charges,” and 
03.54.080, “South Trunk Sewer Area Impact Fee,” of the SMMC and adds Section 7.38.065, “Wastewater Capacity Charge,” 
to establish a new consolidated wastewater capacity charge. The proposed Resolution establishes the Wastewater 
Capacity Charge fee amounts by use, wastewater flow, and wastewater strength loadings.
Art in Public Places
The City has been assessing an Art in Public Places fee since 2005. This fee, which is codified in Chapter 23.60 of the 
SMMC, applies to commercial and multi-family projects with a building permit valuation that is greater than $3M. Art in 
Public Places is an in-lieu fee imposed pursuant to the City’s police power as opposed to a development impact fee 
imposed pursuant to AB 1600.  Because it is an in lieu fee, the developer can work with the City and the Civic Arts 
Committee to provide art on premises to receive credit against the fee or pay into the Art in Public Places Fund in lieu of 
providing art.  In reviewing the costs and needs of the City’s Art in Public Places Program, staff and consultants determined 
that the City was undercollecting for the Art in Public Places fee. The proposed Ordinance amends Section 23.60.060 of the 
SMMC to provide that the fee amount be adopted by City Council resolution. The proposed Resolution establishes the fee 
amount at 1.19 percent of the total building valuation, excluding land acquisition and off-site improvement costs, as noted 
in the nexus study.
NEXT STEPS:
The proposed Ordinance will take effect 60 days after adoption and the Resolution will take effect upon the effective date 
of the Ordinance or 60 days after adoption, whichever is later. In the interim, staff will also continue to work on two 
related efforts:
1.
Staff will continue to pursue potential fee reductions or waivers for affordable housing projects and are currently 
collecting feedback from developers on several policy options. Staff will return to Council in the next few months 
to discuss any findings and make any necessary amendments to the fee schedule.
2.
The proposed changes to the Park Impact and In-Lieu Fees, which were reviewed in Matrix’s nexus study, require 
more extensive revisions to the City’s Municipal Code. Staff will bring the proposed changes to these two fees 
back to Council at a later date.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The nexus reports included as Exhibits A and B to the proposed Resolution provide details on the types of infrastructure 
and services that the City could fund with each impact or in-lieu fee. Exact revenues will depend on the amount of future

CITY OF SAN MATEO
construction.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
In accordance with California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines, section 15378(b)(4), this action is not a project 
subject to CEQA because the adoption or amendment of fees is a fiscal activity not involving commitment to any particular 
project.

which these fees and service charges are to be levied and the City’s revenue sources was made available to the public by

place of this meeting, including a general explanation of the matters to be considered, was published in the San Mateo 
Daily Journal. No requests for mailed notice or renewal requests were received within the past year as required by
